    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

  <span id="freeText17164068472722379403" style="display:none">Half Summer faery princess, half human, Meghan has never fit in anywhere. Deserted by the Winter prince she thought loved her, she is prisoner to the Winter faery queen. As war looms between Summer and Winter, Meghan knows that the real danger comes from the Iron fey—ironbound faeries that only she and her absent prince have seen. But no one believes her.<br /><br />Worse, Meghan's own fey powers have been cut off. She's stuck in Faery with only her wits for help. Trusting anyone would be foolish. Trusting a seeming traitor could be deadly. But even as she grows a backbone of iron, Meghan can't help but hear the whispers of longing in her all-too-human heart.</span>

<div id="review_111582038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111582038" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1594906-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252264728p2/1594906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111582038?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/1594906-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8526821-the-iron-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1594906-kim?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1594906-kim?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111582038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9202672881781201573">I wasn't sure if I was going to give it 4 or 5 stars, because this book is very good, but it does has one mayor flaw that I found to be annoying.<br/><br/>Meghan and Ash. When you think about it... What does she really know about him, besides that he's gorgeous and 'icy'? He tried to kill her several times now. I don't know but that doesn't exactly scream boyfriend material to me. <br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, I nearly creamed myself when I read he has a silver stud in his ear. Add the billowing coat and I'm sold. </span>
  <span id="freeText9202672881781201573" style="display:none">I wasn't sure if I was going to give it 4 or 5 stars, because this book is very good, but it does has one mayor flaw that I found to be annoying.<br /><br />Meghan and Ash. When you think about it... What does she really know about him, besides that he's gorgeous and 'icy'? He tried to kill her several times now. I don't know but that doesn't exactly scream boyfriend material to me. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I nearly creamed myself when I read he has a silver stud in his ear. Add the billowing coat and I'm sold. But having those kind of feelings for somebody who is still a stranger smells a little too much like Bella &amp; Edward to me. <br /><br />To give you an idea of how bad it was sometimes... I'm into romance and I go aaaawwww and OMG! every time a guy in a book does something even remotely cute/sweet/romantic. But there was a part where I laughed out loud; This was me being very inappropriate. Like laughing at a funeral inappropriate. I won't give away any details, but there is a scene where Ash is standing there while Meghan and her entourage are running through a door. When Meghan looks back, the door is falling shut and she sees Ash standing there with (I forgot the exact wording) a trace of a single tear frozen to his cheek. I think even Ironhorse would have hidden under the bed when he heard me laughing. It was a <i>little</i> bit too much. I know, I'm horrible. It should have been pretty and amazing and all... To me it was just cheesy, over the top and hilarious. But! *very serious face* The situation was very very grim and I did feel sad about what was happening. But that specific part... Nah. It didn't work for me.<br /><br />However, I like Ash a lot and I also liked the way this book ended, even if it was pretty predictable. (yes, I'm a very complicated creature)<br /><br />I adore Ironhorse. I liked him in The Iron King (when he speaks, his voice booms in my head, I love it) and now he's one of my favorite characters in The Iron Daughther. Grim still takes the lead though ^^.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9202672881781201573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_297625345" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297625345" />
    <a title="Haleema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema"><img alt="Haleema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402430795p2/4336293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/297625345?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haleema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haleema" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema">Haleema</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=not-again">not-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=stupid">stupid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=great-world-building">great-world-building</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=great-writing">great-writing</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297625345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13340165579283112522">Beware of spoilers!<br/><br/>What a complete disappointment compared to the utter bliss I felt from the first one. Meghan is the reason why I gave this book a two! I shall proceed to have my fangirl moments and my complaints now:<br/><br/><u>Fangirl moments:</u><br/>1. You see, the first 114 pages were decent. However, I must say I had a deep longing to see my Puck! I couldn't stand it. I did not laugh or giggle once throughout the beginning, considering that Prince Ash is an absolute bore.<br/><br/>When Puck finally made his grand entr</span>
  <span id="freeText13340165579283112522" style="display:none">Beware of spoilers!<br><br>What a complete disappointment compared to the utter bliss I felt from the first one. Meghan is the reason why I gave this book a two! I shall proceed to have my fangirl moments and my complaints now:<br><br><u>Fangirl moments:</u><br>1. You see, the first 114 pages were decent. However, I must say I had a deep longing to see my Puck! I couldn't stand it. I did not laugh or giggle once throughout the beginning, considering that Prince Ash is an absolute bore.<br><br>When Puck finally made his grand entrance as a raven on page 115, I shrieked and proceeded to do my happy dance. Finally, some action and humor! <br><br>2. I also had my fangirl moment when Puck and Meghan kissed. It wasn't awkward! Well, if you completely disregarded the fact that Grimalkin claimed that they were humping like rabbits on the bed. Besides that, I thought it was sweet. Before that, I was utterly furious at Meghan for romantically turning to Puck after being turned down by Ash. I wanted to strangle her with her own hair and dump her into a river. She's so unbelievably selfish when it comes to Puck and <i>only</i> Puck. All she--- Okay. I apologize. This is my fangirl section. I shall continue about this later. See how hard it is for me just to fangirl without having my complaints spill out of me?<br><br>3. Ironhorse! I absolutely loved him!<br><br><u>Complaints:</u><br>1. Meghan's obsession over Ash: Besides Puck's heartbreaking absence in the first 114 pages, I was completely annoyed by Meghan's constant, "Where is Ash? The Winter Prince stole my heart. I loved him. Where is Ash? Knives stabbed my heart as I watched him walk away. I love him! I couldn't stop thinking about him." Ash this. Ash that. Ash. Ash. Ash. "I turned to see if Ash was there or not. I turned to see if Ash was waiting for me or not."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372835i/726215.jpg" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I <i>do not</i> need to read about your constant:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380372835ra/726216.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>How long have they known each other?<br><br>2. The whole "I'm treating you like horse crap because I have to, not because I want to" concept is very exhausting. Seen it before over and over again. And Meghan crying over him and believing that Ash's love for her was false and blah, blah, freaking, blah. He treats her like crap and she cries over it instead of telling him off. That is one of the reasons why I do not want Ash and Meghan as a couple. Besides the fact that they bore me to sleep with their "chemistry", they are just not right for each other.<br><br><b>"We cannot be together. Stay away from me. There are too many barriers." shamefully = </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372835i/726217.jpg" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>3. Ash is <i>clearly</i> still in love with Ariella. He thinks about her everyday of his life. He compares her to Meghan. He keeps her personal items with her. He is a destroyed prince who is "in love" with a half-breed only becomes she slightly reminds him of his old love. And of course Meghan is absolutely fine with that because she's head-over-heels with him. Idiocy. <br><br>4. The love triangle. Why must there be a love triangle? I should have known this would happen, though. I was praying to myself that somehow Meghan would end up with Puck, because he's such an awesome beast that always made her laugh and made her comfortable. BUT NO. <br><br><b>The love triangle = TWILIGHT<br>Meghan turning to Puck because she's depressed over Ash = TWILIGHT</b><br><br>5. Meghan sometimes befuddled me with her stupid remarks. One time, I just wanted to smack her across her head with my book.<br><br>A conversation between Ironhorse and Meghan. This is after Ironhorse kills a pixie that was trying to rip Meghan's head off.<br><br><i>"You didn't have to kill it. It was like three inches tall!"<br>"IT ATTACKED YOU. IT CLEARLY HAD AGGRESSIVE INTENT. MY MISSION IS TO PROTECT YOU UNTIL WE RETRIEVE THE SCEPTER. I WILL ALLOW NOTHING TO BRING YOU HARM. THAT IS MY SOLEMN VOW."<br>"Yeah, but you don't need a machine gun to kill a fly. Iron horse killed this teensy little faery---"</i><br><br>So when a knight dies, she's okay with it, but when a little pixie dies, she cries about it? Thank God Grimalkin was there to shout at her for being so stupid and ungrateful that such an enormous creature wanted to protect her. See, Meghan was decent in the first book. She wasn't stupid. Then Ash came along and flipped her brain upside down so that all her cells fell out. <br><br><u>My secret hopes:</u><br><br>1. Despite the fact that Meghan has now returned to her mortal world, I want a new faery to arrive and steal Puck's heart away. She could be anyone. I just want Puck to be with someone who makes Puck their first choice, not second! I just don't want Puck still pining for Meghan at the end of the series. He's Robin Goodfellow hello! Meghan can live happily ever after with her prince, but Puck needs someone better than Meghan.<br><br>Someone like... Tiaothin! Eh, eh?<br><br>They'd be awesome together! Although, we haven't seen much of her we can conclude that they're both mischievous, sly, and so beastly. I wonder if anyone else ships them? Phin! No, really. I want them together. Really. I'm Sirius Black. <br><br>Overall, I am very disappoint, son. This is not how a sequel should be. I just wasn't as happy with this once as I was with <i>The Iron King</i>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3312033397682863352">I'm beginning to really appreciate reading a series where all the books are out. Aww look at me and these wise life decisions. But anyway! <b>I quite enjoyed this one too!</b> The stakes weren't as personal to my soul (since book 1 was all about Meghan saving her little brother vs this one is just ya know...stopping the destruction of all the fey who are horrible anyway but apparently Meghan is much nicer than I'll ever be) but I enjoy literally every breath that Puck and Ash take.   <span id="freeText3312033397682863352" style="display:none">I'm beginning to really appreciate reading a series where all the books are out. Aww look at me and these wise life decisions. But anyway! <b>I quite enjoyed this one too!</b> The stakes weren't as personal to my soul (since book 1 was all about Meghan saving her little brother vs this one is just ya know...stopping the destruction of all the fey who are horrible anyway but apparently Meghan is much nicer than I'll ever be) but I enjoy literally every breath that Puck and Ash take. Oh and there's *waves vaguely* Meghan too I guess. But pUCK AND ASH.<br /><br /><b> ➸ PLOT</b><br />Like I said, super high stakes since we're stopping all of faery land from destroying itself in a war. But they're literally like a writhing mass of 5 year olds and they're BORED and have viciously wicked magic they want to use. I can't even. Every page with him is a blessing.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b> ➸ MY FEELS</b><br />I have feels. Definitely more than 3. Maybe even 5. It's fun, it's not stressful, it has a lot of old tropes that I laugh softly at but also somewhat enjoy. Except it's as WHITE as WHITE BREAD and this is tiresome. &gt;_&gt; <br /><br />bUt anyway. People get hurt and stabbed, there are surprising deaths, blood everywhere, creepy iron fey doing their creepy stuff, and yay!! Fun times!! I love everything except Meghan wow sorry about that!! (could she just take charge of her own fate pls)</span>

<div id="review_2019131977" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2019131977" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2019131977?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8526821-the-iron-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=childhood-loves">childhood-loves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=kidnapped">kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=hate-that-i-love-them">hate-that-i-love-them</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=read-listened-with-my-kids">read-listened-with-my-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2019131977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16485807331527197477">The second book in 'The Iron Fey' series, 'The Iron Daughter' definitely had my attention from start to finish. I'm a sucker for angst and emotional pain in my romances. This book was jam-packed with both. However, it also had a healthy dose of action for the adventure junkies out there.<br/><br/>'The Iron Daughter' begins with Meghan in captivity at the Winter Court. Ash has transformed into someone unrecognizable, denying any feelings for Meghan and turning his back on her. As his antics become crueler,</span>
  <span id="freeText16485807331527197477" style="display:none">The second book in 'The Iron Fey' series, 'The Iron Daughter' definitely had my attention from start to finish. I'm a sucker for angst and emotional pain in my romances. This book was jam-packed with both. However, it also had a healthy dose of action for the adventure junkies out there.<br /><br />'The Iron Daughter' begins with Meghan in captivity at the Winter Court. Ash has transformed into someone unrecognizable, denying any feelings for Meghan and turning his back on her. As his antics become crueler, Meghan is forced to come to terms with the possibility that she never really knew Ash at all.<br /><br />Appearances aren't always as they seem though. This is a lesson that Meghan learns time and time again as she attempts to navigate the politics and manipulative games of the Winter Court. The sadistic tendencies of the court members may be the only thing that Ash was fully honest about.<br /><br />As you can probably guess already, Queen Mab played a much more significant role in this book. Prince Ash's brothers were also introduced, making the story more multidimensional. Each has their own motives for their actions and their own agenda. The same is true for multiple characters in the Winter Court that also enter the picture during this book.<br /><br />Eventually, all hell breaks loose. Meghan and Ash are thrust back together by circumstance. Ash is faced with the same feelings of betrayal that Meghan had been forced to cope with when the tables are turned on him. There's nothing quite like the harsh sting of betrayal to put things in perspective. <br /><br />While there was plenty of angst and adventure to keep me engaged, I'd be lying if I said that there wasn't something that drove me crazy with this series. This series featured one of my biggest pet peeves in a story, beginning in the first book and only becoming more pronounced in subsequent books--the "perfect, dead ex-girlfriend". Every time I heard Ariella's name I wanted to scream, "Marsha, Marsha, Marsha!". Seriously! Who can compete with the beautiful ex-girlfriend that is canonized upon death? Nobody - that's who! <br /><br />In spite of the infuriating fixation with the dead ex, I still found this book to be a fantastic read overall. Aimed toward a younger audience than most of my book choices, I was able to listen to this story with my kids. Other than a few "mild" naughty words (no f-bombs or anything), there was no content that was concerning or too controversial for them to hear. In fact, it was kind of provided some insight into my fifth-grade daughter's blossoming interest in boys. I'll just say that I wasn't the only one in the car that was sick of the repeated mentions of the "perfect" Ariella.<br /><br />As expected, the book doesn't offer a lot of resolution. One adventure comes to a close and readers are primed for another one to begin. Luckily, I didn't start this series until all of the books had been released so I was able to jump into the next one immediately. Otherwise, the wait might have killed me. <br /><br />I listened to this book in the Audible format and I have to say that the narration was superb. I really enjoyed the voices for each character and the emotional responses of the characters was almost tangible. If you're an audiobook listener, I'd definitely give this audiobook a shot.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16485807331527197477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5135751696074249598" style="display:none">This book is so compelling and exciting! So much so that I <i>need</i> to share with you a detailed summary of the plot. <div id="review_96805655" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96805655" />
    <a title="The Flooze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze"><img alt="The Flooze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599955192p2/355739.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96805655?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Flooze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Flooze" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze">The Flooze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=vanquished_2011">vanquished_2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=ya_teen">ya_teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96805655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7350542806434483810">**6.12.2011 ETA: Finished book three and this is one of the most frustrating YA series I've read to date. If you've no tolerance for angsty, bratty, obtuse heroines, steer right clear of it.**<br/><br/><br/>When I first read <i>The Iron King</i> I enjoyed it. I found Ash intriguing, Puck endearing, Grim deliciously mysterious, and the iron fey’s origins refreshing. I applauded Kagawa for conceptualizing a breed of fey borne of our obsession with technology. I noticed obvious similarities between <i>The Iron King</i> and the</span>
  <span id="freeText7350542806434483810" style="display:none">**6.12.2011 ETA: Finished book three and this is one of the most frustrating YA series I've read to date. If you've no tolerance for angsty, bratty, obtuse heroines, steer right clear of it.**<br /><br /><br />When I first read <i>The Iron King</i> I enjoyed it. I found Ash intriguing, Puck endearing, Grim deliciously mysterious, and the iron fey’s origins refreshing. I applauded Kagawa for conceptualizing a breed of fey borne of our obsession with technology. I noticed obvious similarities between <i>The Iron King</i> and the movie Labyrinth, but they didn’t prevent me from appreciating the story as a whole. <br /><br />Time passed and friends read the book. In their reviews I found references to other works - plot points they’d come across before in movies, books, and manga - and I decided to lower my rating. Nevertheless, I still clung to the idea that these concerns fell into the FBS zone. Surely the second book would heighten my opinion of the series and distinguish it from other YA.<br /><br />It surely did not.<br /><br /><b>Though I still enjoy the concept of the iron fey and the destruction their technology brings to a magic-dependant realm, <i>The Iron Daughter</i> was such a frustrating read that I may abandon the series.</b> My exasperation can be summed up in one word: Meghan.<br /><br /><b>Apparently, our heroine is a fickle, emotionally-charged idiot.</b> Time and again, her angsty cries defy all logic and she comes off as completely self-absorbed. Some examples? Gladly. (Slight spoilers for the trajectory of the romance.)<br />- Ash explains he cannot show kindness towards her at Mab’s court because any weakness will be preyed upon. Yet when he publicly behaves in a boorish manner, she decides that he played her, anguishes over his rejection and begs him to snatch her up in an embrace in front of all of Winter. Waaah, I thought I was special, she cries. Guess that warning went in one ear and out the other. He shouldn’t have wasted his breath. <br />- Ash makes an attempt to rescue her from Mab’s cruelty. Meghan chooses this tense, time-sensitive occasion to have a hissy fit in a hall, putting them at risk of getting caught. This is made all the worse by her <i>admission</i> that she’s being an idiot, preventing me from ever having any sympathy for her again.<br />- Meghan learns of numerous precautions Ash put into place (at great risk to himself) to ensure her well-being, yet she <i>still</i> considers the possibility that he used glamour to manipulate her affections.<br />- And the most confounding moment: Her love, <i>for whom her soul was crying</i> earlier on, sits in a corner dying. Instead of heeding Puck’s repeated statement that the boy needs a healer, Meghan takes the time to browse her CD collection and interrogate a bogey. Zero sense of urgency. But when they reach the healer, she bullies the woman into helping because her darling man doesn’t have much time left. Where was this fearsome concern over the passage of time, this “heart-twisting” worry, when she was quizzing the bogey under the bed?<br /><br />Add to this the <b>all too common love triangle</b>. Not two minutes after going into a lengthy tirade about how she longs for Ash, Meghan actually thinks, “Why not try with Puck?” Why is this convention so frequently used in YA? Are teen emotions really this changeable in the writer’s eyes? In my experience, it’s the opposite. When a teenager finds someone to pine over, crush on, lust after they become absolutely fixated. Especially when the object of fixation is set in a Romeo and Juliette, us against the world, light. <br /><br />Moreover, what do Puck and Ash see in her? <b>It’s a common complaint across the UF genre: too often writers create a heroine with multiple suitors, only to fail to justify her allure to the reader.</b> Other than Meghan’s odd powers and her unthinking willingness to tumble headlong into trouble, there’s nothing that sets her apart. The only character whose fascination I can understand is Grim - for him, it’s like a front row seat at a train wreck or the Jerry Springer show. Why shouldn’t he amuse himself?<br /><br />As an aside, <b>Puck and Ash’s relationship is far more deserving of discussion</b> than Meghan’s relationship with either. As one character observes: “They’re either best friends or darkest enemies, I can’t tell which.” Neither can we, since they’re the embodiment of the fine line between love and hate. Forget Meghan - these two boys are perfect fodder for some slashy fanfic (making mental note to check the interwebs later). <br /><br />Back to <b>Grimalkin. These characters would be dead - many times over - without his help.</b> He repeatedly pops in at the eleventh hour to save them, picking up the slack in their poorly conceived plans. Grim’s disdain-riddled comment that Ash, Meghan and Puck are “the hope of the NeverNever” is all too valid. With these illogical, inept children next in line to take up the mantle, Faery seems doomed regardless.<br /><br />Grim’s timely interventions raise another problem: <b>convenient plot points abound</b>. Kagawa also frequently halts the action so she can insert some new twist, leading to <b>scenes that feel forced and unnatural</b> in context (a day trip to a spa comes to mind - frankly, every scene with the new character, Lea, seems out of place). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I can’t get over the fact that Meghan’s Winter Formal just happens to take place while they’re in the real world, allowing Ms. Social Outcast to attend with not one but <i>two</i> attractive boys. Ah, a Cinderella moment. Not cliché at all. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>I remain impressed with Kagawa’s flair for economical yet highly-detailed descriptions of settings, but why must she resort to stale repetition for characters’ appearances and emotions? Disappointing.</b><br /><br /><b>Were this series a trilogy, I would willingly pick up the next book for the resolution of the iron fey plot.</b> After all, the developments on that front were enough to keep me reading this installment. However, I notice that there is a fourth book on the horizon, and who knows how many more to follow. At this juncture, <b>I’m not convinced the series is deserving of the time investment</b>. Meghan sets my teeth on edge, and I can’t imagine her improving. This is going on the Maybe Later pile. Way, <i>way</i> later.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7350542806434483810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2949832171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2949832171" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30999560-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593744134p2/30999560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2949832171?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/30999560-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781426864155" href="/book/show/8645360-the-iron-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=teen-drama">teen-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=cheesy-romance">cheesy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=too-much">too-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=forgettable">forgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30999560-maria?shelf=trashy-pleasure">trashy-pleasure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2949832171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10992356067850602078">Worst piece of garbage I have read in years.<br/><br/>That's the TL;DR version of the review. The longer version is a lengthier rant of sorts so strap on, if you're ready!<br/><br/>You would think the sequel could not get much worse considering the first book had already a bunch of cliches, but somehow... just somehow it beats it by far. The Iron Daughter is full of predictable "twists", there is absolutely no mystery in anything, because everything is so obvious from the moment the first hint comes up, but of cour</span>
  <span id="freeText10992356067850602078" style="display:none">Worst piece of garbage I have read in years.<br /><br />That's the TL;DR version of the review. The longer version is a lengthier rant of sorts so strap on, if you're ready!<br /><br />You would think the sequel could not get much worse considering the first book had already a bunch of cliches, but somehow... just somehow it beats it by far. The Iron Daughter is full of predictable "twists", there is absolutely no mystery in anything, because everything is so obvious from the moment the first hint comes up, but of course every single character in the book has as much brains as a mouse so for the entirety of the book, you see them bring up important details but conveniently NEVER discuss them again so you always have intelligent conversation that go something like:<br /><br />"What do we do now?"<br />"I don't know. We have no power and nothing could help us."<br />"Oh my God, we are so powerless."<br />"We are, yes! Let's hope luck is in on our side!"<br /><br />And of course luck always is and at the last moment that important detail comes up again and somehow everyone is surprised. Literally, I do not know how someone can write such slow characters? The writing is awful in basically every aspect.<br /><br />Meghan in this wonderful book acts like the stupidest, boy-crazed person around without really realizing the dangers when she should, but only complains why Ash isn't giving her his utmost attention and she has the gal to compare other fae sticking to Ash as "high school mean girls". You are a Class A high school girl, Meghan! Her development? None. She keeps being boy-crazed, pulling Puck into the mix, even though EVERYONE knows her final pick so the triangle isn't even a triangle and then as always, she ignores all the important details for the "plot"'s sake. She uses a special kind of power a couple times now, but she never really thinks on working it. EVEN BY THE END OF THE BOOK when she has done so much more. She is one of the worst main characters I've ever read.<br /><br />The boys are inconsequential. Puck gets way mor annoying in this book, always trying to be funny when the situation has nothing to do with it and it's just cringy and Ash is Ash, the emo boy who keeps going back and forth in his decisions. I actually feel sorry for him that is stuck with Meghan. <br /><br />Now the development of the story... had potential, but ends up atrocious, because the main priority is fanservice. Nevermind we have an impeding war and we are trying to beat the Iron Fae that no one believes they exist, but we have to put there random romantic moments between Meghan and Ash, even though there is literally no need. Ash needs a large capacity of human emotion? Turn invisible and sit at the corner of. Jesus. Do we really need to make this a big deal? <br /><br />And not only that but the single character that I liked was killed off. I guess it's better to be dead that be in this book and risk getting Meghan-level stupid, but still, my only hope!<br /><br />Either way, I have way too much gripes for many details of the story such as the war seemingly taking forever to start even though the march started right away, to Oberon barely having any line in 2 whole books (he's basically a prop for Meghan at this point), to side characters barely offering any value to the plot, to Grimalkin always licking his paws like it's the only thing he can do and how he seems to be the only smart entity around and should have no reason to hang out with them as he lost more favors than gained, to how trods are so easily found, to how they always meet the right person for help, to every single thing they do. But I digress.<br /><br />Will I continue? I'm not sure. I want to for completion's sake, but I didn't expect things to go from bad to soo much worse so fast. The only thing that has it going for it is the identity of the false king, who apparently no one cared to ask who it was so it's not secret because they are hiding it, but because characters can't even ask "Who is in charge this time?"</span>
  <a data-text-id="10992356067850602078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_95870349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95870349" />
    <a title="Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/180315-sophie-riggsby-allthingsequilateral"><img alt="Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556432497p2/180315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95870349?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral" href="/user/show/180315-sophie-riggsby-allthingsequilateral">Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/180315-sophie-riggsby-allthingsequilateral?shelf=dont-tell-others-youre-my-fave">dont-tell-others-youre-my-fave</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/180315-sophie-riggsby-allthingsequilateral?shelf=hot-boys-with-swords">hot-boys-with-swords</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95870349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9124035047341108386">See I have a thing about sequels -- they either hit the mark or they don't. There's no in-between point, at least not for me.<br/><br/>And I loved <i>The Iron King's</i> mythology, charcters and plot, so I did have to wonder could Julie Kagawa do that all over again? Well,YA Fantasy Fans, she did even more!<br/><br/>What I loved about <i>The Iron King</i> was the mythology -- the nod to traditional faerie lore and then the completely justified and believable addition of an Iron Court. This tilted the familiar power struggle betw</span>
  <span id="freeText9124035047341108386" style="display:none">See I have a thing about sequels -- they either hit the mark or they don't. There's no in-between point, at least not for me.<br /><br />And I loved <i>The Iron King's</i> mythology, charcters and plot, so I did have to wonder could Julie Kagawa do that all over again? Well,YA Fantasy Fans, she did even more!<br /><br />What I loved about <i>The Iron King</i> was the mythology -- the nod to traditional faerie lore and then the completely justified and believable addition of an Iron Court. This tilted the familiar power struggle between the Seelie and the Unseelie Courts and created complete chaos. It was exhilirating to read through it. But now what?<br /><br />Well, Julie answered that question. She answered it in spades. When we last left Meaghan and Ash they were on their way to Ash's home, The Winter Court. Not exactly the turf that a Summer Court Princess (albeit half-human, half-fey) would feel comfortable in but Meaghan had made a promise to Ash and to the fey, promises are everything.<br /><br />I'm going to keep this review spoiler-free, so let me just say that the book may start off with the fulfillment of a promise but where it leads you is so unbelievably unexpected that you will be gasping out loud. I've read a few books like this, so chock full of action that you find it exhilirating to turn the pages only to discover that there's even more. Isn't that the best part? I'm going to take a moment and compare Julie's action writing sequences to those of my favorite YA fantasy author, Cassandra Clare. Yes, they are THAT good. That unbelievably good.<br /><br />But that's not the best part. The very best part were the characters' arcs -- Meaghan's, Ash's and Puck's. Their back-stories, journeys and amazing transformations were so credible that I found my heart aching for them.<br /><br />And please, don't even ask if there's romance. There is unbelievable, forbidden, beautiful romance. Again, my hat's off to Julie, who wrote the scene on page 99 so well, that I had to text a few of my close bookwormish pals just to vent. What did the text say, you ask? It said, "He's breaking my heart, but in a good way."<br /><br />A full five-stars to Julie Kagawa's <i>The Iron Daughter</i>. If you love action, romance and watching how characters mature through heart-wrenching trials, you will love this story as much as I do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9124035047341108386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_827043178" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/827043178" />
    <a title="Lazaros" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros"><img alt="Lazaros" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578697302p2/22313662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/827043178?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lazaros" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lazaros" href="/user/show/22313662-lazaros">Lazaros</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer827043178" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6043682266149066749">Fey, Fae, whatever you choose to call them, they are amazing, and while I haven't read so many books with fae, I am always astounded by the amazing stories they make up for.<br/><br/>This one was a suprise. The first one, it was really good but I never thought I'd give the next one 5 stars, but it really was amazing so I couldn't help but giving the highest rating there is. <br/><br/>So, the book picks up from where it left off in the first book. Ash delivers Meghan to the Unseelie Court. What happens next is for y</span>
  <span id="freeText6043682266149066749" style="display:none">Fey, Fae, whatever you choose to call them, they are amazing, and while I haven't read so many books with fae, I am always astounded by the amazing stories they make up for.<br /><br />This one was a suprise. The first one, it was really good but I never thought I'd give the next one 5 stars, but it really was amazing so I couldn't help but giving the highest rating there is. <br /><br />So, the book picks up from where it left off in the first book. Ash delivers Meghan to the Unseelie Court. What happens next is for you to find out. I'll just say that there are betrayals, and a known-to-you-someone is rising to take Machina's place, which is just bad bad news. <br /><br />Like the first one, this was full of adventure. It's really fast-paced and while for some the fast-pace thingy doesn't work, I love it when it's well-executed. <br /><br />Meghan has lost her powers so she's kind of at the mercy of the other's help. Not that I'm complaining about her companions. Puck blew me away, this guy, always grinning, always being the positive one, he's just amazing. And my heart is breaking for him... You know why.<br /><br />Ash, the icy prince, well, he's not going to be icy for long. <br /><br />The romance is heating up, the adventure got better, the plot thickens, the characters are wonderful. These are the reasons why I gave this 5 stars and I really hope to give the next one 5 stars as well. </span>

<div id="review_309576559" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309576559" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309576559?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-totally-saw-that-coming">i-totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=hand-me-some-tissues">hand-me-some-tissues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=take-your-insta-love-and-leave">take-your-insta-love-and-leave</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=judge-a-book-by-the-cover">judge-a-book-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=read-reviewed">read-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309576559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15072251977152143306">I feel very conflicted at the moment, because I don’t know what rating to give this. The story itself was pretty good, and the ending was sweet, but it’s just Meghan… I don’t think I can <i>not</i> take stars away from this book because of Meghan… I did some thinking about it, and figured without Meghan, this book probably would have gotten three and a half stars from me. With Meghan, I’ve come to the conclusion that it gets two and a half stars. I don’t know if that’s too much, and I’m being too gener</span>
  <span id="freeText15072251977152143306" style="display:none">I feel very conflicted at the moment, because I don’t know what rating to give this. The story itself was pretty good, and the ending was sweet, but it’s just Meghan… I don’t think I can <i>not</i> take stars away from this book because of Meghan… I did some thinking about it, and figured without Meghan, this book probably would have gotten three and a half stars from me. With Meghan, I’ve come to the conclusion that it gets two and a half stars. I don’t know if that’s too much, and I’m being too generous, or if I'm taking too much from the rating, but that was the final rating I decided. Now, let’s get this review started. <br><br>What should I start off with, the good, or the bad? I have a <i>lot</i> to write about the bad of this book, so maybe we should start with the good and get it over with. <br><br><u>What I liked in The Iron Daughter:</u> <br><br>1: First, I’ll say that I’m team Puck. I don’t think that will change, no matter what. Despite this, I did like Ash a lot more in this book. I really didn’t like him too much in the first book, and I thought he was a total ass. I think it was really smart of Kagawa to expand on the backstory of Ash and Ariella’s love, and how she showed that Ash still kept Ariella’s belongings, and that he really, truly loved her. <br><br>2: The kiss! Not between Ash and Meghan, I’m against that relationship, but between Meghan and Puck! While I think Meghan only did it because she was lonely and Ash wasn’t there, I was still really happy for Puck. He deserves some happiness, after being there for Meghan for so long, and then one boy comes along and tries to kill Meghan and she loves him instead. How could you not feel bad for Puck in that situation? <br><br>3.: Grimalkin! I love you Grimalkin, you’re awesome, witty and funny. I better see more of you in the other books or I will <i>not</i> be a happy camper. <br><br>Well... It looks like that’s it for the things I liked in The Iron Daughter. (Yikes!) Now, moving onto the things I didn’t like (and the things I hated). It might get ugly. Fangirls/boys may want to turn away. Especially if you like Meghan. <br><br><u>What I didn’t like or hated in The Iron Daughter</u><br><br>1: <s>Bella Swan</s> Meghan Chase<br><br><img height="250" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374630ra/728800.gif" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, wait… I may have to break that down for Meghan. <br><br>I’m. calling. you. <i>stu-pid</i>. <br><br>Do I have to speak slower, or did you get that, Meghan?<br><br>Oh, but you're not just stupid. You're also selfish. And whiny. And obsessive. And naïve. And so <i>freaking</i> pathetic. <br><br>Do I need to go on? Because I can. <br><br>My question to you, dear, dear Meghan is, why go for the boy who wants to kill you, and was insulting you throughout the whole 25% of the book. And let me tell you, Ash's "I'm treating you like crap because I have to because I don't want to look bad in front all my all mighty mother" is not a good excuse. It's a horrible excuse. And when he does this you don't just <i>cry</i> over the fact that he might not love you like you love him, and that he used you. You slap him silly! (And, odds are, <i>no</i> men are going to love you as much as you loved Ash in such a short amount of time. Take this advice, Meghan. You're only going to scare more men off). Sure, you went all “I hate Ash”, and “Ash is a heartless, arrogant bastard. I hate him.”, but none of that counts if, in the next page, you’re declaring your undying love for him. Also, when someone says the word "Prince" to you, don't respond with, "What prince? <i>My</i> prince?". He's not <i>your</i> prince. You don't own him, even though it seems you think the contrary. <br><br>With all her whining and obsession over a boy wanting to kill her, I felt that Meghan became the Bella Swan of the Fey. Then she thought this, and I was certain she was the Bella Swan of the Fey:<br><blockquote>Sometimes I dreamed that Ash was in my room, standing in a corner or beside my bed, just watching me with his bright silver eyes.</blockquote><br>....Wait, what? <br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364457i/716151.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then she starts doubting herself, blaming herself because she thinks Ash hates her, and I just wanted to shake the living crap out of her. Does it matter if he hates you? You should really be focusing on the biggest task at hand. <br><blockquote>Ash despised me. Everything he'd said and done was to bring me to his queen. He was a cheat. He'd used me, to further his own ends. And the saddest part was, I still loved him.</blockquote><br>You're right, Meghan. That is pretty sad. At least you can admit it. <br><br>But then, Meghan, you got all jealous. You couldn't take the fact that Ash still loves his dead girlfriend, and the fact that he mourns over her and thinks of her constantly. I think this might have been the point where my hatred for Meghan truly formed. It sickens me to think that Meghan was deliberately trying to get in between Ash and Ariella's relationship, and that she was jealous of his mourning over her. I didn't know someone could be so shallow until I read that. <br><br>My hatred of Meghan pretty much expanded from there, especially when she went with Ash and left Puck. I can't even describe how bad I felt for Puck. (like I mentioned earlier in the review, he's always been there for her, and the fact that she's siding with a boy who's tried to kill her on multiple occasions must've hurt). <br><br>The many stupid decisions of Meghan Chase eventually led to a school dance, where she met up with Scott. You know Scott. The boy who took a picture with Meghan and photoshopped it into a naked picture and sent it to the whole school in book one? I was so happy when Meghan saw Scott there. I thought there would be some slapping, some cursing, some defending herself... <br><br><b>
  <i>What the hell was I thinking?</i>
</b><br><br>I mean, seriously. We're talking about Meghan Chase. The Bella Swan of the Fey. I don't even know why I got my hopes up in thinking she'd stand up for herself and pour punch on Scott, or something like that. To be honest, I would've been happier if she just passed him by and sent him an evil glare, but seriously? You're going to have a dance with the freaking kid? And he doesn't even remember who you are? You can seriously let what he did to you go and <i>dance</i> with him? I was just... I couldn't even believe what I was reading. I knew Meghan was stupid, of course, but I didn't know she was <i>that</i> stupid. Still longing to dance with Mr. Popular, I see. Nothing's changed. <br><br>And then she sees Ash flirting with some girls and starts crying, at which point I was laughing at how pathetic she was. You're not even his girlfriend, stop crying. It doesn't make me feel empathy towards you, it only makes me laugh at you.<br><br>I won't be starting <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8685612.The_Iron_Queen__The_Iron_Fey___3_" title="The Iron Queen (The Iron Fey, #3) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Queen</a> right away; I think I need a break from Meghan's stupidity for a little bit. I'll be back, though, and I will continue and eventually finish this series. If Meghan's as stupid in the other books as she was in this one, it won't be easy. <br><br>But, I guess this is our goodbyes, Meghan. I'll... miss you... <br><br><img height="178" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380374630ra/728801.gif" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15072251977152143306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1211555020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1211555020" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1211555020?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8526821-the-iron-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1211555020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15336895915886006096"><b>*** 2.75 ***<br/><br/>A Buddy Read with the awesome MacHalos!!! </b><br/><br/>This could have been so much better than it is... I don't know, maybe it is a case of "it is not you, it is me" situation, but I didn't really enjoy it at all... I appreciate the thought and work that has gone into creating the book and the series as a whole and the previous book was not bad at all, but this one somehow took the air out of my enthusiasm for it. It could also have to do with the type of relationship that is portrayed in this v</span>
  <span id="freeText15336895915886006096" style="display:none"><b>*** 2.75 ***<br /><br />A Buddy Read with the awesome MacHalos!!! </b><br /><br />This could have been so much better than it is... I don't know, maybe it is a case of "it is not you, it is me" situation, but I didn't really enjoy it at all... I appreciate the thought and work that has gone into creating the book and the series as a whole and the previous book was not bad at all, but this one somehow took the air out of my enthusiasm for it. It could also have to do with the type of relationship that is portrayed in this very serious and angsty manner. If Meghan was my daughter or a friend, I would have shaken the heck out of her when she decided to sacrifice not only her own life, but that of many others, when she decided that the boy she has kissed once and known for couple of days is the love of her life and she would do literally anything to save him. I mean anything - she would start a war, give herself to the Devil, choose anything that would be destructive and stupid, she was ready to do for this teenage hormonal crush!!! Maybe that is romantic for some and I might have perceived it as romantic when I was a preteen, but from my life experience right now, this seems ridiculous and irresponsible! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"..."“I know you'd risk everything to protect us, and that's what worries me. You still don't know enough about this world to be properly terrified. Things are going to get screwed eight ways from Sunday, and you're making goo-goo eyes at the enemy! I heard what happened in Machina's realm and yes, it scared the hell out of me. I love you, dammit. I'm not going to watch you get torn apart when everything goes bad.”..."</i>
</b><br /><br />The writing itself was very nice, the story setting had a magical and whimsical feel to it, but the romance was just plain dumb! On top of that, a good friendship was ruined when the friend came out and said he is in love with her, thus making it a love triangle for no particular reason. There was enough drama and angst in the romance front already, no need to add a third love interest in there... <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"..."“I can't forget. I miss him. I know he's the enemy, and we broke all kinds of rules, but I don't care. I miss him so much, Puck."..."</i>
</b><br />The characters did not win me over either. Meghan is the princes of reckless decisions and angst, Prince Ash is a brooding emotional pit, Queen Mab was a balloon filled with bravado, King Oberon was just there, no personality whatsoever, Puck was OK, but clearly unbelievable for his supposed "love" for a stupid little girl, and the exiled Queen was just too one-sided... Thank goodness for Grimalkin and Ironhorse, who were able to bring some soul and dimension to the group. I would not mind adding them to my menagerie of favorite Magical Animals from Fantasy Books:):):)<br /><br />Overall, I think the people who will enjoy this book fully are the ones wit a bit less .... life experience than me, let's say preteens and teens. It would be perfect for them, but I believe it looses its powers of magic on the rest of us:):):) No, we are not old, just have had some of those angst-inducing love affairs a few to many times to want to willingly root for another one of those in an imaginary scenario:):):) I wish the youngsters to enjoy and read with abandon!!! <br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and may you always find what you need in the pages of a good Book!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15336895915886006096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322866217" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322866217?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=me-likey-mucho">me-likey-mucho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=3-to-4-stars">3-to-4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=they-are-so-cute-its-unbearable">they-are-so-cute-its-unbearable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322866217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13474563966089260950"><b>Final rating: 3.5/5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376685ra/731670.gif' width='400' height='175' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731671.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>I am so impressed because this was just soooooooo much more interesting and better than the first one. This was just coooooool ♥ </b>(while we are at it, i dont even know how to write this review properly).<br/><br/>So...before you read this one, <b>i suggest you read the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8070049.Winter_s_Passage__Iron_Fey___1_5_' title='Winter's Passage (Iron Fey, #1.5) by Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>Winter's Passage</a> </b>which is kind of necessary because it shows how Ash feels for Meghan and his warnings to her about Winter's court (which she, of course,<i> ignores</i>) and the trip to the Winter's court, with a danger around</span>
  <span id="freeText13474563966089260950" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 3.5/5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376685ra/731670.gif" width="400" height="175" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731671.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I am so impressed because this was just soooooooo much more interesting and better than the first one. This was just coooooool ♥ </b>(while we are at it, i dont even know how to write this review properly).<br><br>So...before you read this one, <b>i suggest you read the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8070049.Winter_s_Passage__Iron_Fey___1_5_" title="Winter's Passage (Iron Fey, #1.5) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter's Passage</a> </b>which is kind of necessary because it shows how Ash feels for Meghan and his warnings to her about Winter's court (which she, of course,<i> ignores</i>) and the trip to the Winter's court, with a danger around. <br><br><b>Anyway, i adored the story for this one </b>- it was exciting even though in the beginning it was frustrating a little because of Meghan, but afterwards it just got better and better. Many things happened, and new characters appeared (like Leanan-whatever-her-name-is)and some old characters were back (like IRONHORSE).<br><br>And some parts of the book surprised me because i didn't expect it, and it was quite interesting. AND i loved the end of the book ♥<br><br>And, after this book i am 100% Team Ash, because he is just..... fabulous??? And Puck is back in this book and kicking assess and being sarcastic and all - and i know he loves Meghan too, but Meg really loves Ash so it makes it awkward... sigh...<br><br><blockquote> <b>► CHARACTERS</b>: </blockquote><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Meghan &amp; Ash</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br>Meghan is faced with harsh reality when she comes to the Winter court. <br>Everyone ridicule her, make her life miserable, and she faced the worst betrayal of them all - Ash had reverted to his cold state and abandoned her. Or so she thinks. She is just too devastated to think properly and it makes her miss the obvious: that he was doing everything in his power to protect her. And it took a while for her to actually understand that *sigh*... But in the second half of the book she gets a little bit stronger and less weepy character because she finally got a grip of things around her. There is a threat in the realm and its hard to prove it when you dont have any evidence...<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"What do you want of me, Meghan?" he asked, a low thread of anguish flickering below the surface.<br>Tears blurred my vision, all the fear and heartache of the past few days rising to the surface. "Just you," I whispered. "I just want you."<br> </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Meghan...oh Meghan. She should have gotten an award for these:<br>-being incredibly stupid at times;<br>-incredibly naive;<br>-incredibly frustrating;<br>-incredibly emotional.<br>But, i like her nonetheless, and even though she is incredibly innocent kind of girl, i dont hate her or anything. But i really hope she grows up in the next books.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731671.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> "They only see this outer shell, not who I really am, beneath. You have. You've seen me without the glamour and illusions, even the ones I show my family, the farce I maintain just to survive. You've seen who I really am, and yet, you're still here." </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Meanwhile, Ash is torn between his loyalty and his feelings. He knows that everything in his life will fall apart if he stays with Meghan; his life would never be the same and it makes it even harder for him to decide...But he loves Meghan truly and he is afraid of hurting her... And even though i wanted to slap him and kick his ass for being completely unreasonable, i still love him ♥<br><br><b>(SPOILERS!!!!) </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Ash said he loved Meghan in front of everyone, i was trully surprised. Especially since it earned him <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ banishment for him and Meghan  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and i thought he was going to go back to his mother because it meant everything to him. It seems he is not mama's boy anymore :D  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. O_o.....<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731671.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Puck</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “You're kind of blind, you know?" Puck whispered, smiling to soften his words. "I wouldn't defy Oberon for just anyone. But, for you..." He leaned forward, touching his forehead to mine. "I'd come back from the dead for you.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>So, our glorious sarcastic warrior of Summer has returned! In this book, we find out his true feelings for Meghan, and even though i know he doesn't stand a chance, i am sad, because he deserves a little happiness too. I also loved his relationship with Ash, how they are somewhere in between between friends and enemies ♥<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731671.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Everyone else</u>
  </i>
</b>:<br><br>☻<b> Grimalkin </b> for one, is back and he still rocks. I have no idea what they would do if it werent for him - because he always saves the day in the end. <br>☻<b> Mab</b> turned out to be as cold as i expected and in short: i dont like her at all.<br>☻<b> IRONHORSE</b> IS AMAZING WITH ALL HIS SHOUTING AND NOT KNOWING HOW TO SPEAK WITHOUT SHOUTING HAHAHAHAHHAHA. I liked him a lot :)<br>☻<b> Leanansidhe</b> is interesting and cool, but also scary as hell O_O<br>☻<b> Charles(MAJOR SPOILER)</b> : <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I started suspecting that i knew who he was.....He recognized Meghan but forgot everyone else...and then, the truth was out and it was just like i thought: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ He is Meghan's father who raised her before he disappeared....because Leanansidhe took him and made him crazy...Poor guy :*( <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><blockquote> <b>► OVERALL</b>: </blockquote><br><br>Fabulous continuation to the story - if you can survive Meghan's idiocy at the beginning of the book. I loved it nonetheless and i cant wait to start third book with high hopes for it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380376685i/731671.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
