<div id="review_114637893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114637893" />
    <a title="Yin Chien 인첸" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2944417-yin-chien"><img alt="Yin Chien 인첸" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322927134p2/2944417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114637893?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yin Chien 인첸" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yin Chien 인첸" href="/user/show/2944417-yin-chien">Yin Chien 인첸</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114637893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7598880390475096439">I had high expectations for this book even before I started reading it due to its brilliant debut. I wasn't the least bit disappointed with The Iron Daughter. It was as good as The Iron King, if not better. They story has a powerful and thrilling plot which brings readers on a journey to retrieve the Scepter of Seasons which was stolen by a new kind of Faery called The Iron Fey.<br/><br/>The beginning of the story started with Meghan staying in Tir Na Nog, the Winter Court, where Queen Mab is the monarch.</span>
  <span id="freeText7598880390475096439" style="display:none">I had high expectations for this book even before I started reading it due to its brilliant debut. I wasn't the least bit disappointed with The Iron Daughter. It was as good as The Iron King, if not better. They story has a powerful and thrilling plot which brings readers on a journey to retrieve the Scepter of Seasons which was stolen by a new kind of Faery called The Iron Fey.<br /><br />The beginning of the story started with Meghan staying in Tir Na Nog, the Winter Court, where Queen Mab is the monarch. She feels bad because of the incessant chill, but she feels even worse by Prince Ash's sudden change of behaviour --- he becomes distant, cold and cruel.<br /><br /> His eyes glittered as he shot me a glare of pure loathing. "It's Master Ash, or Your Highness to you, half-breed. And I don't recall giving you permission to speak to me. Remember that, because the next time you forget your place, I'll remind you with my blade." --- Ash, page 28<br /><br /><br />Meghan can't go home, and her father, King Oberon has no way to free her because she is there on a contract of her own free will. When some Iron Fey lead by Tertius steals the Scepter of Seasons and murders the crown prince of the Winter Court, Sage, Queen Mab is furious and she accuses Oberon of doing the act of crime. A war is about to start... and Meghan is going to do anything to stop it from happening.<br /><br />I love Julie's hauntingly beautiful description of the scenery of Faeryland. She manages to create a place where beauty and danger coexists. Julie's exquisite literary prose is one of the reasons which makes this book stand out from the sea of other novels in the fantasy genre. Her words made me delve into the Fey world with ease, following Meghan and her friends on their exciting and dangerous adventure.<br /><br />In this novel, Meghan turns to Puck for company due to Ash's absence and cold demeanor. She finds that she actually has some feelings for Puck as well, but not as intense as the love she had for Ash. On the contrary, Puck is the one who pours out all his love and attention on his Princess, always there to support Meghan whenever she needs him, ever so protective of her.<br /><br /> "You're kind of blind, you know?" Puck whispered, smiling to soften his words. "I wouldn't defy Oberon for just anyone. But, for you..." He leaned forward, touching his forehead to mine. "I'd come back from the dead for you."--- Puck, pg 123<br /><br /><br />The story is divided into 3 parts. The one who stole the scepter was revealed in the end of Part 2, but there is no further information about the new (and fake) Iron King. How will the love triangle between Puck, Meghan and Ash end? When the time comes, who will Meghan choose? Is it the mischievous, caring and reliable Puck, or the cold, quiet and passionate Ash?<br /><br />In the nutshell, The Iron Daughter is awesome! I can proudly announce that I'm now a great fan of Julie Kagawa. You should never miss The Iron Fey Series! I really can't wait to read the third book! *Beams with delight!*<br /><br />Visit my blog for more book reviews: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://the-bookaholics.blogspot.com/">http://the-bookaholics.blogspot.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7598880390475096439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_540668620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/540668620" />
    <a title="Anushka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8377084-anushka"><img alt="Anushka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452007230p2/8377084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/540668620?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anushka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anushka" href="/user/show/8377084-anushka">Anushka</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=overrated">overrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer540668620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9093994434841825604">I don’t think I even qualify to review this book as I gave it up after 100 something pages due to its <b>sheer stupidity.</b> I liked its prequel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_' title='The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Iron King</a> just fine, it was better than other YA Fae books in comparison, at least.<br/><br/>In this book it was as if Meghan’s character had taken a complete U-turn. She wasn’t your kick-butt heroine in the first book either but she was even worse in this. Firstly, I had mentioned the same in my review of 1st book as well - that Meghan and Ash didn't exactly lack </span>
  <span id="freeText9093994434841825604" style="display:none">I don’t think I even qualify to review this book as I gave it up after 100 something pages due to its <b>sheer stupidity.</b> I liked its prequel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_" title="The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron King</a> just fine, it was better than other YA Fae books in comparison, at least.<br /><br />In this book it was as if Meghan’s character had taken a complete U-turn. She wasn’t your kick-butt heroine in the first book either but she was even worse in this. Firstly, I had mentioned the same in my review of 1st book as well - that Meghan and Ash didn't exactly lack chemistry; let’s just say that <b>they didn't have any chemistry!</b> I have no clue what they found attractive about each other, their love just...happened, because it was <i>supposed</i> to happen.<br />Ash is described as a handsome silver-eyed Winter prince who has this whole bad-boy thing going which is freakin’ hot, I know that. But it doesn't mean that you fall in love with the guy even though he hasn't even looked at you properly once.<br /><br /><b>If you found their love story absurd in 1st book, you’ll find it insanely bizarre in this one. </b><br /><br />Okay, so Ash and Meghan confessed their dopey love for each other but then Ash told her not to trust his actions in the Winter Land because he needed to pull on a façade of being a perfect prince so he could protect her. <br />Why can’t that snotty little Meghan understand that? He told her <u>several times</u> not to talk to him or express any kind of relation for these many reasons but that twit didn't get a thing in her thick-head! She goes all <i>“I love you, Ash, but you lied to me, Ash. But I’ll still love you, Ash, and you’ll keep lying to me, Ash”!</i> <br /><br />First, Ash’s cocky attitude was getting on my nerves. His vow to be a dick in the name of "protecting" her was totally half-baked and obviously backfired because Meghan the numbnut couldn't keep her mouth shut. She just assumed that Ash never really loved her, he used her to bring her to Unseelie court and blah blah....Sooo doesn't that mean she should actually hate him for doing this to her instead of pining <i>even more</i> for him? That is just <b>ridiculous!</b> I was driven up the wall because of the way these characters were behaving, one time hot, other time cold. <br /> <br />But one thing I truly appreciate is Julie Kagawa’s setting; she is very true to the Fey folklore and characters. With the inclusion of Iron Fey it becomes even more interesting so I’m gonna catch up with this book’s plot somehow and try to read next one properly (maybe). I hope its better or else I am saying goodbye to this series even though I really wanna know how this Iron and Fey business ends.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1104269648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8805084056401807433">Wow. I feel like <b>I. just. can't. get. enough. of. this. world.</b> As I was travelling through Nevernever, following <s>Ash</s> Meghan's steps, my wonder never <i>ever</i> faded. My dear friends who took part in Chelsea's birthday's buddy read can attest how much I got lost in this outstanding world, my heart <i>aching</i> to come back there. <b>I fell in love with every single character I met</b>, from this yawning, infuriating and hilarious Grimalkin to the giant spiders who... Wait, no. I'll follow Meghan on this : <br/><br/><b>"I could</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8805084056401807433" style="display:none">Wow. I feel like <b>I. just. can't. get. enough. of. this. world.</b> As I was travelling through Nevernever, following <s>Ash</s> Meghan's steps, my wonder never <i>ever</i> faded. My dear friends who took part in Chelsea's birthday's buddy read can attest how much I got lost in this outstanding world, my heart <i>aching</i> to come back there. <b>I fell in love with every single character I met</b>, from this yawning, infuriating and hilarious Grimalkin to the giant spiders who... Wait, no. I'll follow Meghan on this : <br><br><b>"I could handle goblins and bogeymen and evil, flesh-eating horses, but giant freaking spiders? That's where I drew the line"</b><br><br>I couldn't agree more. <i>What? Have you seen their legs?</i><br><br>Are you ready to go? Yes? Okay then.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419987663i/13152701._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>"Now, listen. Whatever you see in there, don't buy anything, don't offer anything, and don't accept anything, no matter how much you want it. The vendors will try to make a deal with you - ignore them. Keep silent, and keep your eyes on me. Got it?"</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419987663i/13152702._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Julie Kagawa's writing manages to describe perfectly every single creature we meet, making them <i>fleshed out</i>, so much that I could totally see them jumping out the page and appear in my living-room <i>for real</i>. <br><br><b>"An ancient gnome stared up at me, her face wrinkled and shriveled like a valnut under a frayed clump of white hair. Barely two feet tall, dressed in a once-white robe with tiny gold glasses on the end of her nose, she glared at me like a furious midget bear, black eyes snapping with irritation."</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419987663i/13152703._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As the characters, none of the different settings are rushed : from Queen Mab's palace to the <i>Between</i>, via the High-School, all the places are filled with tiny details which let the world literally <i>appear</i> in front of our wide-eyed eyes. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419987663i/13152704._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>That says it all. Grimalkin, remember?<br><br><b>"How do you know your way around this place, Grim?"<br>Grimalkin blinked. "I am a cat," he said, and vanished down one of the tunnels."</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419987663i/13152705._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Remember <b>Ash</b>? Yeah? That icy Prince I decided to <i>not</i> ramble about in my review of <i>The Iron King</i>? If I thought he won me in that first book, that's nothing in comparison to the way I felt and fell for him in that one. Forget all the broody and wounded male-lead you know : none of them can beat him. Seriously : It took him only <i>one</i> apparition to warm my heart and send a flutter of emotions through me like crazy. <br><br>Well, I can ramble and ramble over and over again about him, but it'd be completely useless : just keep in mind that <b>he's loyal, heart-breaking, courageous, selfless - he's <i>perfection</i> - but the <i>good</i> kind of perfection, that is to say, the perfect imperfection</b> (and no, the fact he's hot isn't even taken into account).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419987663i/13152706._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Again, the <b>plot</b> was well-wrapped and the story fast-paced, and we're reading as in a run, never resting, always captivated, gasping, sometimes frightened, always mesmerized.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419987663i/13152707._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Oh, and by the way, <b>I like Meghan</b>. Yes she shares many personality traits with other young-adults heroines and yes I could have been annoyed at some point but you know what? I never was. I understand her, I can relate to her (<i>throwing rocks? I could totally do that</i>), I'm proud of her. That's all.</i><br><br><b>"Make your choice."<br>Ash looked at me. I saw pain in his eyes, and a little regret, but they shone with such emotion I felt breathless. "I already have."</b><br><br><i><b>Edit</b> : Okay, so after some remarks I got about Meghan I feel the need to add some thoughts : YES, she isn't our kick-ass heroine, and sometimes she makes mistakes, and she's obsessed with Ash, yes. But <i>COME.ON</i>. All the people who know me know how much I love a strong and fierce heroine who can fight and all that but <b>it's not Meghan</b>. <br><br>Why am okay with it? Because she's our average teenager <b>from the beginning</b> and her characterization is <b>coherent</b>. If she had begun to kick everybody's ass <u>I'd have found <b>this</b> strange</u>. And for the fact she forgives Ash for his behavior? Come on. The <b>contrary</b> would have maddened me - because that's OBVIOUS that his behavior is necessary. I'm not excusing all her actions but come on, give the girl a break (give me a break about her anyway). <br><br>I respect other opinions of course and I even understand them. I get it, really. <b>All of this is my opinion and my opinion only.</b><br><br>Just please leave your advice in the comment section <b>below</b>. No need to send messages to say to me that I'm wrong (see what I said earlier? That's only my opinion, just leave it). Thank you all!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8805084056401807433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71081085?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=own-arc">own-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=signed-books">signed-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71081085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6536358930624998901">I think I might have to move The Iron Daughter to the number one position over The Iron King. This series is one of those that just keeps getting better. I have big hopes for book number three! <br/><br/>The Iron Daughter leaves off right where the The Iron King stops. That being said... You might not want to read the rest of this review if you haven’t read book number one, because it might be a tad bit SPOILERY! <br/><br/>You’ve been warned. <br/><br/>I loved Meghan in the first novel.... but at the beginning of The Iron Da</span>
  <span id="freeText6536358930624998901" style="display:none">I think I might have to move The Iron Daughter to the number one position over The Iron King. This series is one of those that just keeps getting better. I have big hopes for book number three! <br /><br />The Iron Daughter leaves off right where the The Iron King stops. That being said... You might not want to read the rest of this review if you haven’t read book number one, because it might be a tad bit SPOILERY! <br /><br />You’ve been warned. <br /><br />I loved Meghan in the first novel.... but at the beginning of The Iron Daughter I seriously wanted to slap some sense into the girl. Where the heck was that girl at the end of the first book, the one that did what she had to do! The one that had grown more confident and wise! Because she was not there at first. I mean, come on Meghan, I know you are in love with Ash.... but all that stuff that he was telling you about guarding yourself because those fey in his court are viscous creatures and they will just use it against you. He wasn’t just telling you that to hear himself talk... I think old Meghan would have picked up on that. But no instead I got this weenie whiney Meghan. <br /><br />Thank goodness someone hit her over the head and I got old Meghan back! <br /><br />One of my favorite characters in this novel, was one that I didn’t like very much the first time around. And I’m not really going to say much more about that..... don’t want to ruin the surprise! I was totally NOT expecting that. Of course Grim was back and he was as charming as ever. <br /><br />I loved watching Meghan and Ash’s relationship develop in this one.... despite the fact that they simply can not be together, I mean summer and winter just do not mix. It’s fun to see how they try to work above that. Will they end up together against all odds!?!?! Like I’m going to tell you. <br /><br />I should have known that the leading novel would not be the last we saw of the Iron Fey... I totally didn’t predict any of what actually happened. It was much better than what I was anticipating. Although.... my idea of a Meghan and Ash running away together and living happily ever after was just as good! <br /><br />But back to the actual book. The plot was action packed... people er fey dropping like flies... dragons, battles, betrayals... you are in for a ride my fellow reader. I picked it up and just could not put it down. <br /><br />I cannot wait for book three! This series is so good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6536358930624998901" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_117783956" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117783956" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572125481p2/3283298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117783956?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=0-faves">0-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=14-faeries">14-faeries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117783956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17637200192178648579"><b>MINOR SPOILER ALERT</b><br/><br/>Ok, um...let’s see..First off: I really, really liked this one. I absolutely love the world Kagawa has created and all the characters in it (IRONHORSE, YOU SERIOUSLY ROCK!). I love Ash, he makes my stomach do flip flops and my pulse race and I devoured this book just like its predecessor. There’s a but, though. Unfortunately, there were a few things that bothered me.<br/><br/>1. Meghan told Ash too soon that she loved him. I cringed and smacked my forehead when I read that part. They di</span>
  <span id="freeText17637200192178648579" style="display:none"><b>MINOR SPOILER ALERT</b><br /><br />Ok, um...let’s see..First off: I really, really liked this one. I absolutely love the world Kagawa has created and all the characters in it (IRONHORSE, YOU SERIOUSLY ROCK!). I love Ash, he makes my stomach do flip flops and my pulse race and I devoured this book just like its predecessor. There’s a but, though. Unfortunately, there were a few things that bothered me.<br /><br />1. Meghan told Ash too soon that she loved him. I cringed and smacked my forehead when I read that part. They didn’t really know each other at that point and in my opinion it was just way too early to bring out the big guns.<br /><br />2. Meghan was a tad bit too naive for my taste. She started getting on my nerves when she acted all devastated because Ash ignored her as soon as they had reached the Winter Court. She even called him out on it. In front of Mab. I mean, hello-ho? Did she miss the speech Tiaothin gave her about Ash being her mortal enemy and the horrible consequences they’d have to face if anybody found out about their feelings for each other? I wanted to yell at her when she tried to act all cozy with Ash in front of Mab. She endangered him and herself by acting so stupid.<br /><br />3. Ok, now I'm doing this "I’m-wiping-all-emotions-off-my-face* hand gesture and am trying to keep a straight face. <br /><br />So...Meghan, Puck and Ash are stuck in the mortal world at some point and Ash needs to recharge his batteries because he had been hurt pretty badly and is all weak. And how do fearies do that? Right, they need a lot of glamour, meaning they need to take Ash someplace where human emotions are running high. Now they are wondering. . . should they take him to a club maybe? Hmm. . . no. Not a good idea. . . But hey, there’s the Winter Formal at Meghan's old school that night, how very convenient, so why not take him there? No sooner said than done, the Winter Formal it is. The situation is all dramatic, the Nevernever is threatened to be destroyed once and for all and they go to the prom? <i>Seriously</i>??? God, I burst out laughing when I read that part. But that wasn’t all. As it turned out, it got even better.<br /> <br />Alright, so the decision is made, they’re going to the prom and Meghan’s waiting all dressed up for her ice prince to take her out. Then he finally steps into the room and what is he wearing? A white tuxedo. <b>WHITE!!!</b> With a blue tie! <b>A BLUE TIE!!!</b> After that, I couldn’t help but imagine Ash looking something like <a href="http://www.kostuemverleih.com/bilder/Weisser%20Anzug.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> or <a href="http://www.brides-beaux.com/sitebuilder/images/IMG_7369-420x660.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a>. It kinda ruined the moment for me...Really, Mrs. Kagawa can't just go and stuff my insanely hot Ash in a white tux.<br /><br />Ok, that’s it with the nagging :D Apart from this, I really enjoyed Iron Daughter and the awesome ending totally made up for everything. I’m dying to read Iron Queen.<br /><br />I ♥ Ash.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17637200192178648579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=unable-to-suppress-my-disbelief">unable-to-suppress-my-disbelief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=chinese-translation">chinese-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=are-you-kidding-me">are-you-kidding-me</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=fairies-related">fairies-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=bad-bad-bad-romance">bad-bad-bad-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722708123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5997437206803322058">To me, The Iron Daughter is a book ruined by the horror known to readers as silly unrealistic YA <s>romance</s> love triangle.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380746833i/3118734._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Can you see the horror? I think we need an exorcist here...please...somebody, HELP!<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380746833i/3118735.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I actually like the setting about feys, I also like the description about the otherworldly landscapes and the different fey kingdoms, I enjoy the concept about the Iron Feys and the little twists and turns the author had offered.<br/><br/>But what I can't stand is Meghan, the main character, acting like a w</span>
  <span id="freeText5997437206803322058" style="display:none">To me, The Iron Daughter is a book ruined by the horror known to readers as silly unrealistic YA <s>romance</s> love triangle.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380746833i/3118734._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Can you see the horror? I think we need an exorcist here...please...somebody, HELP!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380746833i/3118735.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I actually like the setting about feys, I also like the description about the otherworldly landscapes and the different fey kingdoms, I enjoy the concept about the Iron Feys and the little twists and turns the author had offered.<br><br>But what I can't stand is Meghan, the main character, acting like a whinny, impulsive, lovesick teenager, not to mention she's a total fool to believe in every single thing other people tell her. She's an opened book even after she had been warned not to show her weakness in front of the feys. Last but not least, the love triangle between her, Ash and Puck is sickeningly unrealistic.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380746833i/3118736.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Evil love triangles, stay away from me!!!!<br><br>The romance between Ash and Meghan is so bad that I don't know whether I should LOL or start crying. But eventually I decided crying is more suitable. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380746833i/3118737.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ash and Meghan fall in love? Just...when did it happen!?<br><br>As to Puck, I know from the very beginning he doesn't stand a chance no matter how nice and funny he is, for this dude has 'friend zone' written all over his face.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380746833i/3118738._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Puck is doomed at the very beginning, because there's a LAW for every YA girl to fall in love with the brooding, mysterious bad boy. I'd told you before!<br><br>Plus, I really don't think neither Ash nor Puck act and talk like they're powerful immortals who are hundreds if not thousands years old.<br><br>There're still some plot holes in the story, for example <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Meghan's power is supposed to be sealed off by Queen Mab, supposedly the seal cannot be broken without the help of Queen Mab or Meghan's own father King Oberon; but at the end of the story she can use her power all of a sudden without any explanation. *sighs* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>And the book turns out to be a bit too predictable, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I dare say Meghan will turn out to be Iron Queen later. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's too big of a dead giveaway.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5997437206803322058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1474122386883003809"><b>Let’s be serious: The cat is the true hero in this series.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400036ra/774716.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have a feeling that nobody would get anything done without Grimalkin, or whatever its name was. <br/>Most of this book went something like this: "Hey, let's get ourselves in hopeless situations and wait for the cat to show up and save us."<br/><br/>I'm kidding, of course. This book was really fun. The writing in this is so good; it's so easy to picture the <b>Nevernever</b>. (I don't ever want to go there. Never, ever, ever..)<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400036ra/774717.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It's creepy as hell. And things </span>
  <span id="freeText1474122386883003809" style="display:none"><b>Let’s be serious: The cat is the true hero in this series.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400036ra/774716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have a feeling that nobody would get anything done without Grimalkin, or whatever its name was. <br>Most of this book went something like this: "Hey, let's get ourselves in hopeless situations and wait for the cat to show up and save us."<br><br>I'm kidding, of course. This book was really fun. The writing in this is so good; it's so easy to picture the <b>Nevernever</b>. (I don't ever want to go there. Never, ever, ever..)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400036ra/774717.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's creepy as hell. And things keep being eaten. Yay, mortal world!<br><br>So in this one we have a bit of a love triangle going on (only not really, because we all know who she's going to end up with. Even I do, and I haven't finished the series yet!).<br><br>And even though I'm totally <b>Team Ash</b>, I really like the scenes with Puck, because he has the funniest lines. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400036ra/774718.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I love any scene with <b>Puck and Ash</b> together because they have this really interesting friends/enemies relationship. <br><br>Let's talk about the character NAMES in this series. Every time I came across the name <b>Ironhorse</b>, I giggled. I mean, there you are, picturing some huge guy with dreadlocks who talks in all-caps and then his name is IRONHORSE. <br><b>"Ironhorse wasn't usually polite."</b> <br>Come on. Where else can you find sentences this awesome?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400036ra/774719.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then there's "Leanansidhe", whose name, in my head, sounded something like <b>Leananfdudfjdksf</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400036ra/774720.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This was a fun book (I liked it much more than the first one), and if you're into fairies, you should totally read it. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/504614.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_569076295" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/569076295" />
    <a title="Sabrina " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3536114-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425694026p2/3536114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/569076295?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina " href="/user/show/3536114-sabrina">Sabrina </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569076295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10006291164270922211"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345312ra/699996.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>You're kidding me - right?<br/><br/>That is <b>not</b> how you write a sequel!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380414559ra/817378.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I am <i>beyond</i> disappointed by this novel. It was simply a chore to read. And there is purely 1 reason for my general dislike of the novel:<br/><br/>Megan<br/><br/>A.k.a. The Bella Swan of the Iron Fey series. I couldn't stand to read about her. She was just so irritating. I get it - you're in love with Ash - but I mean, c'mon. Have some self-respect, girl. <br/><br/>Look. I love romance. I'm the romance kinda gal. If there isn't romance in a book, I'll <i>make</i> romance. </span>
  <span id="freeText10006291164270922211" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345312ra/699996.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You're kidding me - right?<br><br>That is <b>not</b> how you write a sequel!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380414559ra/817378.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am <i>beyond</i> disappointed by this novel. It was simply a chore to read. And there is purely 1 reason for my general dislike of the novel:<br><br>Megan<br><br>A.k.a. The Bella Swan of the Iron Fey series. I couldn't stand to read about her. She was just so irritating. I get it - you're in love with Ash - but I mean, c'mon. Have some self-respect, girl. <br><br>Look. I love romance. I'm the romance kinda gal. If there isn't romance in a book, I'll <i>make</i> romance. But I could not take any of the Ash/Megan romance seriously. Her only thoughts about anything were "Boy, he's hot. Dangerous. I shouldn't love him. Ash, I love you!"<br><br>And when he tries to make it clear that he doesn't return her affections, instead of hiking up her skirt and walk out, she sobs. And sobs. <i>And</i> sobs.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399580ra/773471.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Although I am Team Puck, I wouldn't have minded Ash if it had been developed. Instead, I felt the author rushed their romance to the point where it was disbelieving and felt forced. Megan's only known Ash for how long, 6 months? A year, tops? And yet, she's "in love" with him?<br><br>Worse, she becomes whiny and insecure and just weak. I hate weak female characters, they just ugh!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/381074.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>More than half of this book is just her whining about how Ash doesn't love her. That she's second best. Blah. Blah. <b>BLAH</b><br><br>But when she wasn't whining, Ash was. His jealous little mood swings were seriously unnecessary and I just don't see any chemistry between him and Megan. She looks like your ex. That doesn't mean you love her.<br><br>Which brings me to my second largest complaint: The love triangle.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380414559ra/817379.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Excuse me while I barf.<br><br>Did the author seriously have to jump aboard the bandwagon and include a love triangle in her series? Of course she did, why not divide the fans eh?<br><br>Clearly, I'm not a fan of the icy stone-hearted <s>bad-boy-cliche-stock-character-Edward-Cullen</s> prince Ash. I'm a fan of Puck. Why? Easy. He knew Megan longer. He knows how to make her smile. He doesn't toy with her emotions or treat her like crap. <br><br>But does Megan care about any of that? Nope. One look of hottie bad boy and it's bye bye Puck.<br><br>Which totally sucks. Because Puck's my favorite character. And reading about him hurting makes me hurt. I mean - seriously - why can't the best friend get the girl <i>for once</i>?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380414559ra/817380.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Puck, unlike Ash, is a unique character. He would, at least in my opinion, make a much better boyfriend than Ash could ever be.<br><br>But screw Megan. I don't even want her to be with Puck anymore. He deserves better than her whiny little self. <br><br>The ending though. That stupid ending. I just - I can't. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380402913ra/783552.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am so regretful that I paid money for this book, because right now it's shoved in the back of my closet. I don't even know if I want to read the next book after that. My poor baby. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I can't freaking believe that after all that, Megan still joins Ash. She left Puck. He freaking begged her to stay with him and what does she do? Leaves. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380373277ra/726833.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then the author decides to end the book all happy with Ash and Megan being all couple-y and <b>completely</b> ignoring the fact that poor Puck is heartbroken and alone and adfjkdjfkdjsfkjda <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The only reasons I gave this book 2 stars rather than 1 was because of:<br><br>a) Iron horse<br><br>b) Puck<br><br>Iron horse was one of my favorites in the book. As soon as you get past the CAPSLOCK THAT MAKE IT SEEM LIKE IT'S SCREAMING IN YOUR HEAD he's actually a very likable character. <br><br>When Puck (finally) made his appearance, I couldn't stop the grin that appeared on my face. And that kiss ... I enjoyed reading about that kiss. It was very, hot. <br><br>I also enjoyed the continued Iron Fey plot line and concept. The idea is genius, no doubt. Now, if the idea can be the focus and the romance the subplot, then this book would be a winner. <br><br>Overall, I was extremely disappointed with this novel. After enjoying the first book so much, I expected so much of the sequel and was unfortunately let down. I probably will read the next book but I'm not expecting much at all.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/284671.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190621950" />
    <a title="kwesi 章英狮" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4218875-kwesi"><img alt="kwesi 章英狮" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549853625p2/4218875.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13050352720024709570">Promises are not meant to be broken. They are like a glass, they are fragile that one you commit a mistake it will break into little tiny pieces and you must pay for the consequences you have made. After rescuing <i>Ethan</i> from the land of <i>Nevernever</i>, <i>Meghan</i> must pay for the promise she made from the winter prince. She doesn't have a choice but to leave the mortal world and be with <i>Ash</i> in a very cold and dark place, <i>Tir Na Nog</i>.<br/><br/>But when your mortal enemy back and steal a very valuable item that incre</span>
  <span id="freeText13050352720024709570" style="display:none">Promises are not meant to be broken. They are like a glass, they are fragile that one you commit a mistake it will break into little tiny pieces and you must pay for the consequences you have made. After rescuing <i>Ethan</i> from the land of <i>Nevernever</i>, <i>Meghan</i> must pay for the promise she made from the winter prince. She doesn't have a choice but to leave the mortal world and be with <i>Ash</i> in a very cold and dark place, <i>Tir Na Nog</i>.<br /><br />But when your mortal enemy back and steal a very valuable item that increases the power of the season kingdom, everything is in chaos even in the mortal world. The balance had been broke and <i>Meghan</i> has to chase the thief and put it back to the true owner or everyone will die in a very strange way. Can <i>Meghan</i> save the world before everyone dies or she'll die in the hands of the enemies?<br /><br />I don't usually read books in public transit or if I'm travelling but I have to finish this book as soon as possible and I came up with the idea that I'll read the book while travelling for hours. Accidentally, the public train spurt water and I was shock when I saw the book I borrowed from my friend got wet. I don't know what to do and it affects my reading experience completely. I felt so sorry to the owner that I want to change the book with a new one.<br /><br />How come I came up with three stars since I love the first and the novella before <i>The Iron Daughter</i>? I was so shock when I read some parts that are too annoying in my part as a guy. I can't imagine she have to include scenes like make-over, shopping and so on. She's spying but the story's predicament is satisfying the female scene than emphasizing the spying. I don't like to mention where, but seriously it was a no-no for me. After that, I don't know if I have to continue the other books or I'll wait until next year.<br /><br />I also manage to escape my fantasies and I can't connect after reading it again. It was like I'm asking myself if where this story goes. Exactly that she is mixing fairy tales from the book and the fact that her characters' names are very different from the appearance itself. One example is the creature smuggler which was named as Sweet-something and he looks scary and an ogre with that name. <i>Holler!</i> But the name is cute and sweet but not exactly suited to the characters.<br /><br />It means that the book is really for girls, but I object to the fact that this book is written for girls it must be for both sexes. It was just the second book is more girly than the first one, no, I mean, I can't exactly explain it because I have this feelings that the book will be getting better soon like putting more action, gory, or twists that will struggle readers in the end. I keep on reading but it seems that I can't connect to the book. It was like calling someone and the receiver keep on hanging the phone. You want to punch her but you can't and you keep on dialing it until you get annoyed.<br /><br />I also don't like the love or the romance between <i>Ash</i> and <i>Meghan</i>. She was so immature; she keeps on begging for <i>Ash</i> and keeps on crying like a baby. I though she will become more mature in the book after rescuing <i>Ethan</i> in the <i>Nevernever</i> but no, she becomes more childish than before. I also read some reviews and fans keep on smuggling information about the love triangle, and I can't feel it in the story. If people will ask me, what is your least favorite from the series, I won't hesitate to answer <i>The Iron Daughter</i>. I just can't accept that <i>Kagawa</i> broke my heart after all I've done.<br /><br />Review posted on <i>the day that the mighty one will create something surprising.</i><br /><br /><b>Rating</b>: <i>The Iron Daughter (Iron Fey #2)</i> by Julie Kagawa, <b>3 Sweets</b><br /><br /><b>Challenges</b>:<br /><i>Book #252 for 2011</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13050352720024709570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_85752843" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85752843" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=own-copy">own-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=fey-folk">fey-folk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=cover-crazz">cover-crazz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85752843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8356044743295020023">If I could give more stars, I totally would:)<br/><br/>Wow! I'm blown away and in complete awe of this book!<br/>I don't want to say to much about the story itself since everyone just needs to pick this up A.S.A.P, but I will say that it's Incredible!<br/>Julie Kagawa has out did herself. To every reviewer who said <b>The Iron Daughter</b> was better then the first, wasn't kidding! <br/>I am in love with this series, this book, these characters.<br/><br/>With hauntingly rich and vivid writing Julie has once again captured the attention </span>
  <span id="freeText8356044743295020023" style="display:none">If I could give more stars, I totally would:)<br /><br />Wow! I'm blown away and in complete awe of this book!<br />I don't want to say to much about the story itself since everyone just needs to pick this up A.S.A.P, but I will say that it's Incredible!<br />Julie Kagawa has out did herself. To every reviewer who said <b>The Iron Daughter</b> was better then the first, wasn't kidding! <br />I am in love with this series, this book, these characters.<br /><br />With hauntingly rich and vivid writing Julie has once again captured the attention of her readers, giving us a pure and gripping plot that you can't help but devour the minute you touch it. This world is so engaging, entertaining and enchanting that it's hard to get your mind wrapped around it, not that it's difficult, just simply mind-boggling. It is so much fun to read!<br /><br />All your favorite characters are back in all there glory and then some!<br />I am so proud of Meghan, and I love being proud of the characters I read about, so that's a big plus. She's strong and feisty and stubborn and I love that she fights back with everything that she has.<br />I was very torn between Puck and Ash, two of my favorite characters who equally won over my heart. Puck has always been such a dear. Kind, funny and play's the part of "the right one" for Meghan. The sensible choice, the better choice. But with all love triangle, it seems that better may not always be best. Never the less, I love them both, but if it were me, I'd have to go with Ash!<br />Ash, ah Ash, if you loved him before? You'll love him even more! He really went through an emotional hell in this book and I found myself flipping through the pages at a feverish pace to find out what would happen next. He's definitely on my list of favorite book swoon-crushes. Totally and completely love him. I wanna keep him. Mine.<br />Oh, and I so want a cat like Grimalkin!<br /><br />I could go on forever gushing about this amazing book, so I'm just going to say that <b>The Iron Daughter</b> is a fast paced thrill ride with a plot concept that is truly unbelievably brilliant. The romance is a beautiful wonder that makes me smile, and Julie Kagawa is a genius for creating an amazing take on this particular paranormal, it makes me love it when I don't favor it all that much to begin with, so that is really saying something.<br />This is definitely on the top of my list of all time favorites! Loved every second of this epic adventure and I am crazily waiting to see how this beloved series will wrap up in <i>The Iron Queen</i>!!<br /><br />If you haven't read the first one *cough Arlene&amp;Morgan cough* then you need to pick it up! You wont be disappointed!<br /><br />A.Must.Read.!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8356044743295020023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3028585353213449459">1.5 "I'm too old for this shit" stars<br/><br/>It was all so stupid. There's nothing good to say about it. Meghan is a moron. If it wasn't for her merry gang of followers, she either be dead or someone's slave by now. Whenever something happens someone always pops up at just the right time to save her. People continually warn her that Fairyland is dangerous especially since she doesn't know the rules and customs. Apparently she isn't capable of heeding anyone else's advice. She makes one mistake after ano</span>
  <span id="freeText3028585353213449459" style="display:none">1.5 "I'm too old for this shit" stars<br /><br />It was all so stupid. There's nothing good to say about it. Meghan is a moron. If it wasn't for her merry gang of followers, she either be dead or someone's slave by now. Whenever something happens someone always pops up at just the right time to save her. People continually warn her that Fairyland is dangerous especially since she doesn't know the rules and customs. Apparently she isn't capable of heeding anyone else's advice. She makes one mistake after another only digging herself into a deeper hole. Then she seems shocked when the thing that people told her would happen happens.<br /><br />All of the characters act like petulant children. Meghan is young, so it's somewhat excusable. Most of them are supposed to be hundreds or thousands of years old. They're all so rash. Every time their feelings get hurt they immediately lash out. All of them use modern slang and simple language. Maybe it's wrong of me to expect ancient beings to be more sophisticated and cunning.<br /><br />Some things in this didn't make sense. 1) Oberon asked Mab to release Meghan and let her go with him. She said no, and he was basically like well okay and rides off into the sunset. WTF? He is the king of half of fairyland. It's pathetic to give up so easily. Shouldn't someone of his caliber excel at bargaining? 2) Mab said Oberon couldn't have her back because she made a deal with Ash to come to her. Wouldn't that bargain have been fulfilled when she went back with Ash? She didn't specify that she would stay for any length of time. No one ever noticed this. Fae are supposed to be crafty and manipulative and spot pathetic loopholes like that a mile away. 3) When Megan bargained with a fae in the last book and agreed to give up a memory, why is it that she can no longer remember the man she believed to be her father? She got fucking screwed on that deal. IMO that's a lot of memories that were taken, not just one because someone being in a person's life for 10 years comprises far more than one memory. None of these crafty fae saw that something was off with that situation either. <br /><br />The love triangle was one of lamest, most pathetic love triangles ever. It was clear in <i>The Iron King</i> that Puck had feelings for Meghan although it wasn't brought up. She and Ash lusted after each other. Neither of her relationships with them felt solidified romantically. From the start of this she acted like Ash was the love of her life. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She proclaimed very early in the book that she loved him. I was blindsided because she didn't know him well at all. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He had to put on a show and act like he hated her to protect her from his family. She was too stupid to understand what was going on even though he tried to explain how it was going to be beforehand. She was hysterical half of the time, going on and on about how she couldn't be without him. It didn't take long for her to inexplicably develop feelings for Puck, all the while still thinking of Ash. It was resolved at the end and went the way I expected it to, but it would have been so much better if there hadn't been a bunch of bullshit along the way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3028585353213449459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NY+Sjg3dnPFfAm6e3+P2iah8/lA5hWygR0bXLj5deNUPqftctoNVmfgp2v8oFvxWfiMZmPcI4sccOJGf8x6KTw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('48OWyQKq8XBrwIZ9BtVpt/wnP3GlvYcACZXLS+hjAznZ5f8bufQ4GMzrMhzxIGNoKnjYuWswCWdS6436JSDxow==')})
  }
//]]>
